## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Chemical reaction kinetics relates the rate of concentration change to the current concentration (and possibly time for non-autonomous systems), governed by the reaction mechanism and order.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order: dA_dt = c0 * A (linear dependence on concentration)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular or second-order reaction)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order rational: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-Hinshelwood kinetics)
- Second-order rational: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A)**2 (inhibited surface reaction kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic reaction where product catalyzes conversion)
- Competing pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order reactions)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reaction with time-varying rate constant)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order reversible reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with back-reaction or source)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding/reaction)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly changing rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → reaction order identification: dA/dt ~ A^n where n is the molecularity or effective order
- Rational dependence on concentration (A/(K+A)) → enzyme saturation or surface site limitation mechanism
- Product of concentration and complement (A*(c-A)) → autocatalytic or logistic-type reaction where product participates
- Negative rate with positive concentration → reactant consumption; sign of rate law coefficient encodes consumption vs. production
- Explicit time dependence in rate expression → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Rational form with A^n in denominator → product or substrate inhibition mechanism
- Rate proportional to A times a polynomial in A → complex multi-step mechanism reduced to effective rate law
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) → chain reaction mechanism with radical intermediates in quasi-steady state
